## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the time derivative of concentration (dA_dt) as a function of time (t) and concentration (A), which is the core of chemical reaction kinetics. It typically involves finding the rate law governing reactant consumption or product formation, often described by ordinary differential equations capturing reaction orders, time-dependent rate constants, or complex mechanisms like autocatalysis and inhibition.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant reaction rate independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate directly proportional to concentration)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law dependence on concentration)
- Autocatalytic growth: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (rate enhanced by product, limited by available reactant)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2) (rate diminishes at high concentration due to overloading effects)
- Time-varying rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (reaction accelerated by external time-dependent factor like temperature ramp)
- Power-law time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (diffusion or surface-growth controlled kinetics)
- Consecutive generation and decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) - c2 * A (time-dependent source term minus first-order consumption)
- Sigmoidal autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A**2) (cooperative activation with high-concentration saturation)
- Deviation from dynamic equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (relaxation towards a time-shifting equilibrium concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order scaling → Log-log slope corresponds to power-law exponent dA_dt = c * A**n
- Autocatalytic feedback → Rate proportional to product of concentration and remaining capacity dA_dt = c * A * (C - A)
- Induction/delay period → Higher-order concentration dependence A**n (n>1) causing negligible initial rate
- Quasi-steady intermediate → Rational saturation form A/(1+c*A) indicating transient complex equilibrium
- Time-programmed forcing → Separable kinetics f(t)*g(A) where f(t) captures external temperature or pressure ramps
- Parallel pathway competition → Sum of distinct rate terms c1*A**n1 + c2*A**n2 representing multiple simultaneous mechanisms
- Diffusion-limited regime → Fractional time exponent t**0.5 or combined fractional powers in t and A
- Bistable switching → Cubic polynomial nonlinearity A - A**3 or sigmoidal derivative shape indicating multiple steady states

3. A sine of a logarithm term: `+C4 * sin(log(A + 1))`

Many candidates are rational functions or sums of terms. I need to check if they can reduce to the GT form.
The GT has no denominator. So if a candidate has a denominator, the denominator must cancel out with the numerator, or the candidate must be a sum of terms where the denominator is 1.
Wait, the GT is just a sum of three terms.
Let's look at Candidate 8: `A*(A*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)) + c3*sin(log(A + 1))`
Expand: `c0*A^2 + c1*A*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(log(A + 1))`
This matches the structure exactly!
Term 1: `c0*A^2` (matches `-C1*A^2` if c0 is negative)
Term 2: `c1*A*exp(c2*t)` (matches `-C2*A*exp(-C3*t)` if c1 is negative and c2 is negative)
Term 3: `c3*sin(log(A + 1))` (matches `+C4*sin(log(A + 1))`)
So Candidate 8 is a perfect match.

Let's check other candidates just in case.
Candidate 1: Rational function. Unlikely to match unless denominator cancels. Denominator is `(A*c2 + 1)*(A**2*c1 + 1)`. This depends on A, so it won't cancel to a polynomial + exp + sin unless numerator is specifically constructed. But the GT has no A-dependent denominator. So Candidate 1 is NO MATCH.
Candidate 2: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7) + c8/A**(1/3)`
Has `A*c1` (linear term) and `c8/A**(1/3)`. GT has no linear term or inverse cube root. Can we set c1=0, c8=0? Yes.
Then it becomes `c0*A^2 + c2*A*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`.
Can `sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)` match `sin(log(A + 1))`?
`log(A*c6 + 1) = log(c6*(A + 1/c6))`. This is `log(c6) + log(A + 1/c6)`.
So `sin(c5*(log(c6) + log(A + 1/c6)) + c7)`.
To match `sin(log(A + 1))`, we need `c5 = 1`, `1/c6 = 1` => `c6 = 1`, and `c5*log(c6) + c7 = 0` => `c7 = 0`.
So yes, Candidate 2 can match if we set c1=0, c8=0, c5=1, c6=1, c7=0.

So Candidate 2 is a MATCH.

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_t*sin(log(A + c5))

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

This has three terms:
1. A quadratic term: `c₀*A²`
2. An exponential decay term: `c₁*A*exp(c₂*t)`
3. A sine-of-log term: `c₃*sin(log(A + 1))`

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these three basis functions.

**Key observations:** The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a very specific basis function. Most candidates don't have this. Let me quickly scan for candidates containing `sin(log(...))`:

- **Candidate 44**: has `sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1))` ✓
- **Candidate 8**: has `sin(log(A + 1))` ✓

Most other candidates have `sin(A*c + c)`, `exp(A*c)`, `log(A*c+1)`, `A^(1/3)`, `sqrt(A)`, `cos(...)`, etc. These are fundamentally different basis functions from `sin(log(A+1))`.

Let me analyze the promising candidates:

### Candidate 8: `A*(A*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)) + c3*sin(log(A + 1))`

Expanding: `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*sin(log(A+1))`

Comparing with GT: `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A+1))`

Set c0 = -0.16498, c1 = -0.16498, c2 = -0.01276, c3 = 0.6208. **This matches exactly!**

Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 44: `(A*(c0 + (A + c1)*(c2*exp(c3*t) + c4)) + c5*(A + c1)*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1)))/(A + c1)`

Simplifying: `A*(c0/(A+c1) + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1))`

= `A*c0/(A+c1) + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + A*c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1))`

The term `A*c0/(A+c1)` is a rational function, not a polynomial. We need `A²` from the GT. Can `A*c4 + A*c0/(A+c1)` equal `-0.16498*A²`? 

`A*c4 + A*c0/(A+c1) = A*(c4*(A+c1) + c0)/(A+c1) = A*(c4*A + c4*c1 + c0)/(A+c1)`

For this to equal `-0.16498*A²`, we'd need `(c4*A + c4*c1 + c0)/(A+c1) = -0.16498*A`, which means `c4*A + c4*c1 + c0 = -0.16498*A*(A+c1) = -0.16498*A² - 0.16498*c1*A`. This requires an A² term in the numerator, but the numerator is linear in A. So this cannot match.

Candidate 44 verdict: [NO MATCH]
